<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2><A
NAME="dm4315_kraft_foods_inc._and_subsidiar__kra03777"> </A>
<A NAME="toc_dm4315_1"> </A>
<BR></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>Kraft Foods&nbsp;Inc. and Subsidiaries<BR>  Notes to Condensed Consolidated Financial Statements<BR>  (Unaudited)    <BR></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;1.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Accounting Policies:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Basis of Presentation  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
interim condensed consolidated financial statements of Kraft Foods&nbsp;Inc. ("Kraft"), together with its subsidiaries (collectively referred to as the "Company"), are unaudited. It is the
opinion of the Company's management that all adjustments necessary for a fair statement of the interim results presented have been reflected therein. All such adjustments were of a normal recurring
nature. Net revenues and net earnings for any interim period are not necessarily indicative of results that may be expected for the entire year. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>These
statements should be read in conjunction with the Company's consolidated financial statements and related notes, and management's discussion and analysis of financial condition and results of
operations, which appear in the Company's Annual Report to Shareholders and which are incorporated by reference into the Company's Annual Report on Form&nbsp;10-K for the year ended
December&nbsp;31, 2003. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
January&nbsp;2004, the Company announced a new global organizational structure, which resulted in new segments. The Company's new segments are U.S. Beverages&nbsp;&amp; Grocery; U.S. Snacks;
U.S. Cheese, Canada&nbsp;&amp; North America Foodservice; U.S. Convenient Meals; Europe, Middle East&nbsp;&amp; Africa; and Latin America&nbsp;&amp; Asia Pacific. The new segment structure in North America
reflects a shift of certain divisions and brands between segments to more closely align these businesses to consumer sectors. Results for the Mexico and Puerto Rico businesses, which
were previously reported in the Cheese, Meals and Enhancers segment, are now reported in the Latin America&nbsp;&amp; Asia Pacific segment. Also, in connection with the new global organizational
structure, Kraft, in March&nbsp;2004, changed the legal name of one of its subsidiaries, Kraft Foods North America,&nbsp;Inc., to Kraft Foods Global,&nbsp;Inc. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Certain
prior year amounts have been reclassified to conform with the current year's presentation, due primarily to the new global organizational structure. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Stock-Based Compensation Expense  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company accounts for employee stock compensation plans in accordance with the intrinsic value-based method permitted by Statement of Financial Accounting Standards ("SFAS") No.&nbsp;123,
"Accounting for Stock-Based Compensation," which has not resulted in compensation cost for stock options. The market value at date of grant of restricted stock and rights to receive shares of stock is
recorded as compensation expense over the period of restriction. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2004 and 2003, the Company granted shares of restricted stock and rights to receive shares of stock to eligible employees, giving them in most instances all of the rights
of shareholders, except that they may not sell, assign, pledge or otherwise encumber the shares and rights. The shares and rights are subject to forfeiture if certain employment conditions are not
met. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2004, the Company granted approximately 4.1&nbsp;million restricted Class&nbsp;A shares to eligible U.S. based employees and also issued to eligible
non-U.S. employees rights to receive approximately 1.9&nbsp;million Class&nbsp;A equivalent shares. Restrictions on most of the stock and rights lapse in the first quarter of 2007. The
market value per restricted share or right was $32.23 on the date of grant. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
fair value of the shares of restricted stock and rights to receive shares of stock at the date of grant is amortized to expense ratably over the restriction period. The Company recorded
pre-tax compensation expense related to restricted stock and rights of $79&nbsp;million and $27&nbsp;million, respectively, for the nine months and three months ended
September&nbsp;30, 2004, and $43&nbsp;million and $16&nbsp;million, respectively, for the nine months and three </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>10</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<P style='page-break-before:always'></p>
<!-- ZEQ.=1,SEQ=10,EFW="2146084",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=13936,FOLIO='10',FILE='DISK029:[04CHI5.04CHI4315]DM4315A.;12',USER='ABLIJDE',CD=';4-NOV-2004;16:01' -->
<A NAME="page_dm4315_1_11"> </A>
<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>Kraft Foods&nbsp;Inc. and Subsidiaries<BR>
Notes to Condensed Consolidated Financial Statements<BR>
(Unaudited) </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>months
ended September&nbsp;30, 2003. The unamortized portion, which is reported on the condensed consolidated balance sheets as a reduction of earnings reinvested in the business, was
$223&nbsp;million at September&nbsp;30, 2004. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
addition to restricted stock, at September&nbsp;30, 2004, the Company had stock-based employee compensation plans that permit the issuance of stock options to employees. The Company applies the
recognition and measurement principles of Accounting Principles Board Opinion No.&nbsp;25, "Accounting for Stock Issued to Employees," and related Interpretations in accounting for stock options
within those plans. No compensation expense for employee stock options is reflected in net earnings, as all stock options granted under those plans had an exercise price equal to the market value of
the common stock on the date of grant. The following table illustrates the effect on net earnings and earnings per share ("EPS") if the Company had applied the fair value recognition provisions of
SFAS No.&nbsp;123 to measure stock-based compensation expense for outstanding stock option awards for the nine months and three months ended September&nbsp;30, 2004 and 2003: </FONT></P>

<A NAME="page_dm4315_1_12"> </A>
<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>Kraft Foods&nbsp;Inc. and Subsidiaries<BR>
Notes to Condensed Consolidated Financial Statements<BR>
(Unaudited) </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;2.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Asset Impairment, Exit and Implementation Costs:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Restructuring Program:  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
January&nbsp;2004, the Company announced a three-year restructuring program with the objectives of leveraging the Company's global scale, realigning and lowering its cost structure,
and optimizing capacity utilization. As part of this program, the Company anticipates the closing or sale of up to twenty plants and the elimination of approximately six thousand positions. From 2004
through 2006, the Company expects to incur up to $1.2&nbsp;billion in pre-tax charges, reflecting asset disposals, severance and other implementation costs, including an estimated range
of $750&nbsp;million to $800&nbsp;million in 2004. Approximately one-half of the pre-tax charges are expected to require cash payments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the nine months and three months ended September&nbsp;30, 2004, pre-tax charges under the restructuring program of $453&nbsp;million and $45&nbsp;million, respectively, were
recorded as asset impairment and exit costs on the condensed consolidated statements of earnings. These charges resulted from the 2004 announcement of the closing of twelve plants, the termination of
co-manufacturing agreements and the commencement of a number of workforce reduction programs. The majority of the restructuring charges for two of these plants, which are located within
Europe, will be recorded upon local regulatory approval of the plant closures, which is expected in the fourth quarter of 2004. Approximately $167&nbsp;million of the pre-tax charges
incurred during the first nine months of 2004 will require cash payments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Pre-tax
restructuring liability activity for the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2004 was as follows: </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Severance
costs in the above schedule, which relate to the workforce reduction programs, include the cost of related benefits. Specific programs announced during the first nine months of 2004, as part
of the overall restructuring program, will result in the elimination of approximately 2,900 positions. Asset write-downs relate to the impairment of assets caused by the plant closings. Other costs
incurred relate primarily to contract termination costs associated with the plant closings and the termination of co-manufacturing agreements. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Implementation Costs:  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;During the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2004, the Company recorded $26&nbsp;million of pre-tax implementation costs associated with the
restructuring program of which $9&nbsp;million was recorded as a reduction of net revenues, $13&nbsp;million was recorded in cost of sales and $4&nbsp;million was recorded in marketing,
administration and research costs on the condensed consolidated statement of earnings. During the three months ended September&nbsp;30, 2004, the Company recorded $16&nbsp;million of
pre-tax implementation costs associated with the restructuring program of which $9&nbsp;million was recorded as a reduction of net revenues, $3&nbsp;million was
recorded in cost of sales and $4&nbsp;million was recorded in marketing, administration and research costs on the condensed consolidated statement of earnings. These costs include the discontinuance
of certain product lines and incremental costs related to the integration of functions and closure of facilities. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Intangible Asset Impairment Charge:  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2004, the Company completed its annual review of goodwill and intangible assets. This review resulted in a $29&nbsp;million non-cash pre-tax
charge related to an intangible asset impairment for a small confectionery business in the United States and certain brands in Mexico. This charge was recorded as asset impairment and exit costs on
the condensed consolidated statements of earnings. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Total:  </I></FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>These
pre-tax asset impairment, exit and implementation costs, which totaled $508&nbsp;million and $61&nbsp;million, respectively, for the nine months and three months ended
September&nbsp;30, 2004, were included in the operating companies income of the following segments: </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>Kraft Foods&nbsp;Inc. and Subsidiaries<BR>
Notes to Condensed Consolidated Financial Statements<BR>
(Unaudited) </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Other:</I></FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the third quarter of 2003, the Company recorded a pre-tax charge of $6&nbsp;million for asset impairment and exit costs related to the closure of a Nordic snacks plant. This
charge was included in the operating companies income of the Europe, Middle East&nbsp;&amp; Africa segment. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;3.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Related Party Transactions:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>At
September&nbsp;30, 2004, Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. owned 85.1% of the Company's outstanding shares of capital stock. Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc.'s subsidiary, Altria Corporate
Services,&nbsp;Inc., provides the Company with various services, including planning, legal, treasury, accounting, auditing, insurance, human resources, office of the secretary, corporate affairs,
information technology and tax services. Billings for these services, which were based on the cost to Altria Corporate Services,&nbsp;Inc. to provide such services and a management fee, were
$230&nbsp;million and $243&nbsp;million for the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2004 and 2003, respectively, and $73&nbsp;million and $78&nbsp;million for the three months ended
September&nbsp;30, 2004 and 2003, respectively. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>At
September&nbsp;30, 2004, the Company had short-term amounts payable to Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. of $221&nbsp;million. Interest on these borrowings is based on the applicable London
Interbank Offered Rate. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;4. Acquisitions and Divestitures:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2004, the Company acquired a U.S.-based beverage business. During the third quarter of 2003, the Company acquired trademarks associated with a small U.S.-based natural
foods business and in the second quarter of 2003, the Company acquired a biscuits business in Egypt. During the first nine months of 2004 and 2003, total purchases of businesses, net of acquired cash,
were $136&nbsp;million and $97&nbsp;million, respectively. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the third quarter of 2004, the Company sold a snack nuts business in Brazil. During the third quarter of 2003, the Company sold a European rice business. The aggregate proceeds received from
sales of businesses during the first nine months of 2004 and 2003 were $11&nbsp;million and $25&nbsp;million, respectively. The Company recorded pre-tax losses from sales of businesses
of $8&nbsp;million during the first nine months of 2004, and recorded pre-tax gains from sales of businesses of $23&nbsp;million during the first nine months of 2003. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
operating results of businesses acquired and divested were not material to the Company's consolidated financial position, results of operations or cash flows in any of the periods presented. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;6.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Contingencies:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Kraft
and its subsidiaries are parties to a variety of legal proceedings arising out of the normal course of business, including a few cases in which substantial amounts of damages are sought. While
the results of litigation cannot be predicted with certainty, management believes that the final outcome of these proceedings will not have a material adverse effect on the Company's consolidated
financial position, results of operations or cash flows. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Third-Party Guarantees:</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;At September&nbsp;30, 2004, the Company's third-party guarantees, which are primarily derived from acquisition
and divestiture activities, approximated $27&nbsp;million. Substantially all of these guarantees expire through 2013, with $4&nbsp;million expiring through September&nbsp;30, 2005. The Company
is required to perform under these guarantees in the event that a third party fails to make contractual payments or achieve performance measures. The Company has a liability of $21&nbsp;million on
its condensed consolidated balance sheet at September&nbsp;30, 2004, relating to these guarantees. </FONT></P>

<!-- ZEQ.=7,SEQ=16,EFW="2146084",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=932245,FOLIO='16',FILE='DISK029:[04CHI5.04CHI4315]DM4315A.;12',USER='ABLIJDE',CD=';4-NOV-2004;16:01' -->
<A NAME="page_dm4315_1_17"> </A>
<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>Kraft Foods&nbsp;Inc. and Subsidiaries<BR>
Notes to Condensed Consolidated Financial Statements<BR>
(Unaudited) </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;8.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Segment Reporting:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company manufactures and markets packaged food products, consisting principally of beverages, cheese, snacks, convenient meals and various packaged grocery products through Kraft Foods
Global,&nbsp;Inc. and its subsidiaries. Kraft manages and reports operating results through two units, Kraft North America Commercial and Kraft International Commercial. Reportable segments for
Kraft North America Commercial are organized and managed principally by product category. Kraft International Commercial's operations are organized and managed by geographic location. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
January&nbsp;2004, the Company announced a new global organizational structure, which resulted in new segments. Kraft North America Commercial's new segments are U.S. Beverages&nbsp;&amp;
Grocery; U.S. Snacks; U.S. Cheese, Canada&nbsp;&amp; North America Foodservice; and U.S. Convenient Meals. Kraft International Commercial's segments are Europe, Middle East&nbsp;&amp; Africa; and Latin
America&nbsp;&amp; Asia Pacific. The new segment structure in North America reflects a shift of certain divisions and brands between segments to more closely align these businesses to consumer sectors.
Results for the Mexico and Puerto Rico businesses, which were previously reported in the Cheese, Meals and Enhancers segment, are now reported in the Latin America&nbsp;&amp; Asia Pacific segment. The
Company's 2004 and 2003 results by segment are discussed herein under the new reporting structure, and historical amounts have been restated. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company's management uses operating companies income, which is defined as operating income before general corporate expenses and amortization of intangibles, to evaluate segment performance and
allocate resources. Management believes it is appropriate to disclose this measure to help investors analyze the business performance and trends of the various business segments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Interest
and other debt expense, net, and provision for income taxes are centrally managed and, accordingly, such items are not presented by segment since they are not included in the measure of
segment profitability reviewed by management. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Segment
data were as follows: </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the third quarter of 2004, the Company sold a snack nuts business in Brazil and recorded a pre-tax loss of $8&nbsp;million. This loss is included in the operating companies income
of the Latin America&nbsp;&amp; Asia Pacific segment. During the third quarter of 2003, the Company sold a European rice business and recorded a pre-tax gain of $23&nbsp;million. This gain
is included in the operating companies income of the Europe, Middle East&nbsp;&amp; Africa segment. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;9.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Financial Instruments:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the nine months and three months ended September&nbsp;30, 2004, ineffectiveness related to cash flow hedges was not material. During the nine months and three months ended
September&nbsp;30, 2003, ineffectiveness related to cash flow hedges was a gain of $13&nbsp;million, which was recorded in cost of sales on the condensed consolidated statements of earnings. At
September&nbsp;30, 2004, the Company was hedging forecasted transactions for periods not exceeding the next eighteen months and expects substantially all amounts reported in accumulated other
comprehensive earnings (losses) to be reclassified to the consolidated statement of earnings within the next twelve months. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Note&nbsp;10.&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Benefit Plans:</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
December&nbsp;2003, the Financial Accounting Standards Board ("FASB") issued a revised SFAS No.&nbsp;132, "Employers' Disclosures about Pensions and Other Postretirement Benefits." In the first
quarter of 2004, the Company adopted the new interim-period disclosure requirements of this pronouncement relating to net periodic benefit cost and employer contributions to benefit plans, except for
certain interim-period disclosures about non-U.S. plans which are not required until after December&nbsp;31, 2004. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company sponsors noncontributory defined benefit pension plans covering substantially all U.S. employees. Pension coverage for employees of the Company's non-U.S. subsidiaries is
provided, to the extent deemed appropriate, through separate plans, many of which are governed by local statutory requirements. In addition, the Company's U.S. and Canadian subsidiaries provide health
care and other benefits to substantially all retired employees. Health care benefits for retirees outside the United States and Canada are generally covered through local government plans. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Other
expense above is due to additional pension benefits related to workforce reduction programs under the Company's restructuring program. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Employer Contributions  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company presently plans to make contributions, to the extent that they are tax deductible, in order to maintain plan assets in excess of the accumulated benefit obligation of its U.S. funded
plans. During the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2004, $288&nbsp;million of employer contributions were made to U.S. plans. Currently, the Company anticipates making additional contributions
of approximately $2&nbsp;million during the remainder of 2004, based on current tax law. However, this estimate is subject to change due primarily to asset performance significantly different than
the assumed long-term rate of return on pension assets and significant changes in interest rates. In addition, during the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2004, the Company made
pension plan contributions to non-U.S. plans of $175&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
December&nbsp;2003, the United States enacted into law the Medicare Prescription Drug, Improvement and Modernization Act of 2003 (the "Act"). The Act establishes a prescription drug benefit under
Medicare, known as "Medicare Part&nbsp;D," and a federal subsidy to sponsors of retiree health care benefit plans that provide a benefit that is at least actuarially equivalent to Medicare
Part&nbsp;D. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
May&nbsp;2004, the FASB issued FASB Staff Position No.&nbsp;106-2, "Accounting and Disclosure Requirements Related to the Medicare Prescription Drug, Improvement and Modernization
Act of 2003" ("FSP 106-2"). FSP 106-2 requires companies to account for the effect of the subsidy on benefits attributable to past service as an actuarial experience gain and
as a reduction of the service cost component of net postretirement health care costs for amounts attributable to current service, if the benefit provided is at least actuarially equivalent to Medicare
Part&nbsp;D. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company adopted FSP 106-2 in the third quarter of 2004. The impact in the third quarter of 2004 was a reduction of pre-tax net postretirement health care costs and an
increase in net earnings of $12&nbsp;million, which is included above as a reduction of $1&nbsp;million in service cost, $5&nbsp;million in interest cost and $6&nbsp;million amortization of
unrecognized net loss from experience differences. In addition, as of July&nbsp;1, 2004, the Company reduced its accumulated postretirement benefit obligation for the subsidy related to benefits
attributed to past service by $315&nbsp;million and decreased its unrecognized actuarial losses by the same amount. The impact for the fourth quarter of 2004 will be to reduce pre-tax
net postretirement health care costs and to increase net earnings by approximately $12&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Description of the Company  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Kraft
Foods&nbsp;Inc. ("Kraft"), together with its subsidiaries (collectively referred to as the "Company"), is the largest branded food and beverage company headquartered in the United States and
the second largest in the world. At September&nbsp;30, 2004, Altria Group,&nbsp;Inc. held 97.9% of the combined voting power of Kraft's outstanding capital stock and owned 85.1% of the outstanding
shares of Kraft's capital stock. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company manufactures and markets packaged food products, consisting principally of beverages, cheese, snacks, convenient meals and various packaged grocery products through Kraft Foods
Global,&nbsp;Inc. (formerly known as Kraft Foods North America,&nbsp;Inc.) and its subsidiaries. Kraft manages and reports operating results through two units, Kraft North America Commercial and
Kraft International Commercial. Reportable segments for Kraft North America Commercial are organized and managed principally by product category. Kraft International Commercial's operations are
organized and managed by geographic location. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
January&nbsp;2004, the Company announced a new global organization structure, which resulted in new segments. Kraft North America Commercial's new segments are U.S. Beverages&nbsp;&amp;
Grocery; U.S. Snacks; U.S. Cheese, Canada&nbsp;&amp; North America Foodservice; and U.S. Convenient Meals. Kraft International Commercial's segments are Europe, Middle East&nbsp;&amp; Africa; and Latin
America&nbsp;&amp; Asia Pacific. The Company's 2004 and 2003 results by segment are discussed herein under the new reporting structure, and historical amounts have been restated. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
unfavorable impact of asset impairment, exit and implementation costs on net earnings and diluted EPS is due to the following: </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Restructuring Program</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;In January&nbsp;2004, the Company announced a three-year restructuring program. As part of this program,
the Company anticipates the closing or sale of up to twenty plants and the elimination of approximately six thousand positions. From 2004 through 2006, the Company expects to incur up to
$1.2&nbsp;billion in pre-tax charges, including an estimated range of $750&nbsp;million to $800&nbsp;million in 2004. The Company recorded pre-tax asset impairment and
exit costs of $453&nbsp;million for this program. In addition, the Company also recorded $26&nbsp;million of pre-tax implementation costs associated with the restructuring program. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Intangible Asset Impairment Charge</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;During the first quarter of 2004, the Company completed its annual review of its goodwill and intangible
assets. This review resulted in a $29&nbsp;million non-cash pre-tax charge related to an intangible asset impairment for a small confectionery business in the United States
and certain brands in Mexico. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>For further details, see Note&nbsp;2 to the Condensed Consolidated Financial Statements and the Business Environment section of the following Discussion and
Analysis.</I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Lower Effective Income Tax Rate</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;The Company's reported effective income tax rate decreased by 3.2&nbsp;percentage points to 31.9%,
resulting from a $76&nbsp;million favorable resolution of an outstanding tax item in the third quarter of 2004 and the reversal of tax accruals that are no longer required due to tax events that
occurred during the first half of 2004. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Currency</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;The favorable currency impact on net earnings and diluted EPS is due primarily to the weakness of the U.S. dollar versus the euro
and the Canadian dollar. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Operations</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;The decrease in results from operations was due primarily to the following: </FONT></P>

<UL>
<DL compact>
<DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>Lower
income at Kraft North America Commercial reflecting higher commodity costs, increased promotional programs and higher benefit costs, partially offset by higher pricing
and favorable volume/mix.
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>Lower
income at Kraft International Commercial reflecting higher costs, including benefits, promotional programs and infrastructure investment in developing markets. </FONT></DD></DL>
</UL>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>For further details, see the Consolidated Operating Results and Operating Results by Business Segment sections of the following Discussion and Analysis.</I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>See discussion of events affecting the comparability of statement of earnings amounts in the Consolidated Operating Results section of the following Discussion and
Analysis.</I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
unfavorable impact of asset impairment, exit and implementation costs on net earnings and diluted EPS is due to the following: </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Restructuring Program</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;As discussed above, during the three months ended September&nbsp;30, 2004, the Company recorded pre-tax
asset impairment and exit costs of $45&nbsp;million for its restructuring program. In addition, the Company recorded $16&nbsp;million of pre-tax implementation costs associated with
the restructuring program. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>For further details, see Note&nbsp;2 to the Condensed Consolidated Financial Statements and the Business Environment section of the following Discussion and
Analysis.</I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Lower Effective Income Tax Rate</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;The Company's reported effective income tax rate decreased by 6.7&nbsp;percentage points to 28.4%,
resulting from a $76&nbsp;million favorable resolution of an outstanding tax item. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Gains on Sales of Businesses, net</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;The unfavorable impact on net earnings and diluted EPS is due primarily to the 2003 gain on sale of the
European rice business and the 2004 loss on the sale of the snack nuts business in Brazil. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Operations</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;The decrease in results from operations was due primarily to the following: </FONT></P>

<UL>
<DL compact>
<DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>Lower
income at Kraft North America Commercial reflecting higher commodity costs, increased promotional programs and higher benefits costs, partially offset by higher
pricing and favorable volume/mix.
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>Lower
income at Kraft International Commercial reflecting higher costs, including benefits and promotional programs, partially offset by favorable volume/mix. </FONT></DD></DL>
</UL>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>For further details, see the Consolidated Operating Results and Operating Results by Business Segment sections of the following Discussion and Analysis.</I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>2004 Forecasted Results</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&#151;In October&nbsp;2004, the Company announced that it narrowed its 2004 full-year diluted EPS guidance
range to $1.56 to $1.60, including an estimated charge of $0.30 from asset impairment and exit and implementation costs for the restructuring program. The forecasted 2004 diluted EPS also includes a </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>25</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<P style='page-break-before:always'></p>
<!-- ZEQ.=3,SEQ=25,EFW="2146084",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=102423,FOLIO='25',FILE='DISK029:[04CHI5.04CHI4315]DS4315A.;6',USER='SLYUBOM',CD=';5-NOV-2004;13:27' -->
<A NAME="page_ds4315_1_26"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>negative
pre-tax impact from commodities of more than $750&nbsp;million versus last year, due primarily to high costs for cheese, coffee, meat, energy and packaging. The forecasted
diluted EPS also reflects an expected income tax rate of 33% for the year due to the resolution of certain U.S. and foreign tax matters. The Company continues to review its businesses for potential
divestitures and acquisitions, and current forecasts assume no change in the Company's portfolio. The factors described in the section entitled </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Forward-Looking and Cautionary
Statements</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2> of the following Discussion and Analysis represent continuing risks to these projections. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>On
October&nbsp;22, 2004, the American Jobs Creation Act of 2004 was signed into law. The Company is currently reviewing the legislation to determine the impact. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Discussion and Analysis  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B>Business Environment  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company is subject to a number of challenges that may adversely affect its businesses. These challenges, which are discussed below and under the "Forward-Looking and Cautionary Statements"
section, include: </FONT></P>

<UL>
<DL compact>
<DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>fluctuations
in commodity prices;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>movements
of foreign currencies against the U.S. dollar;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>competitive
challenges in various products and markets, including price gaps with competitor products and the increasing price-consciousness of consumers;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>a
rising cost environment;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>a
trend toward increasing consolidation in the retail trade and consequent inventory reductions;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>a
growing presence of hard discount retailers, primarily in Europe, with an emphasis on own label products;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>changing
consumer preferences, including low-carbohydrate diet trends;
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>competitors
with different profit objectives and less susceptibility to currency exchange rates; and
<BR><BR></FONT></DD><DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2>concerns
about food safety, quality and health, including concerns about genetically modified organisms, trans-fatty acids and obesity. </FONT></DD></DL>
</UL>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>To
confront these challenges, the Company continues to take steps to build superior brand value, transform the portfolio, expand global scale, drive out costs and assets, strengthen employee and
organizational excellence, and demonstrate corporate responsibility. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
January&nbsp;2004, the Company announced its adoption of a four-point plan to achieve sustainable growth. The first element of the plan is to build brand value by continuing to
improve its products, to use more value-added packaging, to develop innovative new products, to manage price gaps effectively and to build closer relationships with consumers. The Company currently
anticipates $525 to $575&nbsp;million of increased spending in 2004 over 2003 to manage price gaps, to increase media presence, to drive growth in developing markets and non-measured
channels, to enhance brand equity and to support new products. During the first nine months of </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>26</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<P style='page-break-before:always'></p>
<!-- ZEQ.=4,SEQ=26,EFW="2146084",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=150263,FOLIO='26',FILE='DISK029:[04CHI5.04CHI4315]DS4315A.;6',USER='SLYUBOM',CD=';5-NOV-2004;13:27' -->
<A NAME="page_ds4315_1_27"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>2004,
the Company increased in-market spending by approximately $400&nbsp;million versus the first nine months of 2003. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
second element of the plan is to accelerate the shift in the Company's brand portfolio to address growing consumer demand including products to meet their health and wellness concerns and their
desire for convenience. The Company is reducing trans-fat in its products, marketing its products that are low in carbohydrates, introducing more sugar-free products, and
emphasizing positive nutrition products. The Company is addressing convenience needs by offering more convenient packaging, such as single-serve and resealable packaging, and products requiring
reduced preparation. The Company is also offering packaging that is customized to suit the needs of growing channels of distribution such as supercenters, mass merchandisers, drugstores and club
stores. The Company also plans to shift its portfolio to reflect changing demographics, for example, by expanding the availability of Hispanic products and bilingual packaging. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
third component of the plan is to expand the Company's global scale through international growth, particularly in developing markets. These markets account for approximately 84% of the world's
population and 30% of its packaged food consumption, but only 11% of the Company's 2003 net revenues. The plan calls for the Company to capture the growth potential of its core categories in markets
where it has operations and to expand its core categories into new markets. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>As
the final component of its plan, which is to drive out costs and assets, the Company announced a three-year restructuring program with the objectives of leveraging the Company's global
scale, realigning and lowering its cost structure, and optimizing capacity utilization. As part of this program, the Company anticipates the closing or sale of up to twenty plants and the elimination
of approximately six thousand positions. From 2004 through 2006, the Company expects to incur up to $1.2&nbsp;billion in pre-tax charges, reflecting asset disposals, severance and other
implementation costs, including an estimated range of $750&nbsp;million to $800&nbsp;million in 2004 and $330&nbsp;million to $360&nbsp;million in 2005. Approximately one-half of
the pre-tax charges are expected to require cash payments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the nine months and three months ended September&nbsp;30, 2004, the Company recorded $482&nbsp;million and $45&nbsp;million, respectively, of asset impairment and exit costs on its
condensed consolidated statements of earnings. During the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2004, these pre-tax charges were composed of $453&nbsp;million of costs under the
restructuring program and $29&nbsp;million of impairment charges relating to intangible assets. During the third quarter of 2004, all of the pre-tax charges related to the restructuring
program. These charges resulted from the 2004 announcement of the closing of twelve plants, the termination of co-manufacturing agreements and the commencement of a number of workforce
reduction programs. The majority of the restructuring charges for two of these plants, which are located within Europe, will be recorded upon local regulatory approval of the plant closures, which is
expected in the fourth quarter of 2004. Approximately $167&nbsp;million of the pre-tax charges incurred during the first nine months of 2004 will result in cash payments. During the
first quarter of 2004, the Company also completed its annual review of goodwill and intangible assets. This review resulted in a $29&nbsp;million non-cash pre-tax charge
related to an intangible asset impairment for a small confectionery business in the United States and certain brands in Mexico. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>27</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<P style='page-break-before:always'></p>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Severance costs in the above schedule, which relate to the workforce reduction programs, include the cost of related benefits. Specific programs announced during the first nine
months of 2004, as part of the overall restructuring program, will result in the elimination of approximately 2,900 positions. Asset write-downs relate to the impairment of assets caused by the plant
closings. Other costs incurred relate primarily to contract termination costs associated with the plant closings and the termination of co-manufacturing agreements. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company also recorded implementation costs associated with the restructuring program. During the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2004, the Company recorded $26&nbsp;million of
pre-tax implementation costs, of which $9&nbsp;million was recorded as a reduction of net revenues, $13&nbsp;million was recorded in cost of sales and $4&nbsp;million was recorded in
marketing, administration and research costs on the condensed consolidated statement of earnings. During the three months ended September&nbsp;30, 2004, the Company recorded $16&nbsp;million of
pre-tax implementation costs, of which $9&nbsp;million was recorded as a reduction of net revenues,
$3&nbsp;million was recorded in cost of sales and $4&nbsp;million was recorded in marketing, administration and research costs on the condensed consolidated statement of earnings. These costs
include the discontinuance of certain product lines and incremental costs related to the integration of functions and closure of facilities. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
addition, the Company expects to incur approximately $140&nbsp;million in capital expenditures from 2004 through 2006 to implement the restructuring program, including approximately
$50&nbsp;million in 2004. During the first nine months of 2004, the Company spent $16&nbsp;million in capital to implement the restructuring program. Cost savings as a result of the restructuring
program are expected to be approximately $120&nbsp;million to $140&nbsp;million in 2004, an additional $130&nbsp;million to $150&nbsp;million in 2005, and are anticipated to reach annualized
cost savings of approximately $400&nbsp;million by 2006. All of these cost savings are expected to be used in support of brand-building initiatives. Cost savings during the first nine months of 2004
were approximately $80&nbsp;million. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Fluctuations
in commodity prices can lead to retail price volatility and intensive price competition, and can influence consumer and trade buying patterns. The Company's businesses are subject to
fluctuating commodity costs, including dairy, coffee and cocoa costs. During the first nine months of 2004, the Company's commodity costs on average have been higher than those incurred in 2003 (most
notably dairy, coffee, meat, energy and packaging), and have adversely affected earnings. Dairy costs rose to historical highs during the first six months of 2004, but subsequently moderated to
historical levels. For the full year 2004, the Company expects a negative pre-tax impact from all commodities of more than $750&nbsp;million as compared with 2003. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
the ordinary course of business, the Company is subject to many influences that can impact the timing of sales to customers, including the timing of holidays and other annual or special events,
seasonality of certain products, significant weather conditions, timing of Company and customer incentive programs, customer inventory programs, Company initiatives to improve supply chain efficiency,
including efforts to align product shipments more closely with consumption by shifting some of its customer marketing programs to a consumption based approach, financial situations of customers and
general economic conditions. </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>28</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<P style='page-break-before:always'></p>
<!-- ZEQ.=6,SEQ=28,EFW="2146084",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=920472,FOLIO='28',FILE='DISK029:[04CHI5.04CHI4315]DS4315A.;6',USER='SLYUBOM',CD=';5-NOV-2004;13:27' -->
<A NAME="page_ds4315_1_29"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the first quarter of 2004, the Company acquired a U.S.-based beverage business. During the third quarter of 2003, the Company acquired trademarks associated with a small U.S.-based natural
foods business and in the second quarter of 2003, the Company acquired a biscuits business in Egypt. During the first nine months of 2004 and 2003, total purchases of businesses, net of acquired cash,
were $136&nbsp;million and $97&nbsp;million, respectively. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>During
the third quarter of 2004, the Company sold a snack nuts business in Brazil. During the third quarter of 2003, the Company sold a European rice business. The aggregate proceeds received from
sales of businesses during the first nine months of 2004 and 2003 were $11&nbsp;million and $25&nbsp;million, respectively. The Company recorded pre-tax losses from sales of businesses
of $8&nbsp;million during the first nine months of 2004, and recorded pre-tax gains from sales of businesses of $23&nbsp;million during the first nine months of 2003. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
operating results of businesses acquired and divested in 2004 and 2003 were not material to the Company's consolidated financial position, results of operations or cash flows in any of the periods
presented. However, one element of the growth strategy of the Company is to strengthen its brand portfolios through disciplined programs
of selective acquisitions and divestitures. The Company is constantly reviewing potential acquisition candidates and from time to time sells businesses that are outside its core categories or that do
not meet its growth or profitability targets. The impact of any future acquisition or divestiture could have a material impact on the Company's consolidated financial position, results of operations
or cash flows. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company periodically calculates the fair value of its goodwill and intangible assets to test for impairment. This calculation may be affected by market conditions noted above, as well as interest
rates and general economic conditions. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
2003, the Company had operations and plants or sold products to third-party distributors located in 15 Middle East countries (as defined by the U.S. Department of State, Bureau of Near Eastern
Affairs), including a biscuit business acquired during 2003 in Egypt. In the region, the Company had operations and plants in three countries (Egypt, Morocco and, through a majority owned joint
venture, Saudi Arabia). In addition, the Company sold products to third-party distributors located in 12 of these countries (Algeria, Bahrain, Israel, Jordan, Kuwait, Lebanon, Oman, Qatar, Syria,
Tunisia, United Arab Emirates and Yemen). Revenue generated from operations or sales to the third-party distributors in the Middle East was approximately $230&nbsp;million in 2003 representing 3.3%
of the net revenues of the Europe, Middle East and Africa segment. In 2004, the Company continues to have operations and plants or to sell products to third-party distributors in these countries,
except for Syria, where the Company ceased sales to the third-party distributor early in the year. In addition, in 2004, the Company entered into agreements with third parties for the resale of the
Company's products into Iraq, Libya and Syria. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>In
November&nbsp;2003, the Company was advised by the Fort Worth District Office of the Securities and Exchange Commission ("SEC") that the staff was considering recommending that the SEC bring a
civil injunctive action against the Company charging it with aiding and abetting Fleming Companies ("Fleming") in violations of the securities laws. District staff alleged that a former Company
employee, who received a similar notice, signed documents requested by Fleming, which Fleming used in order to accelerate its revenue recognition. On September&nbsp;14, 2004, the SEC announced
settlement agreements with Fleming for securities fraud and other violations arising from material earnings overstatements during late 2001 and the first half of 2002. The SEC also announced
settlements with three Fleming suppliers and seven supplier employees, including the Company's former employee, for aiding certain of Fleming's violations. On September&nbsp;15, 2004, the staff of
the SEC informed the Company that it does not intend to recommend an enforcement action against the Company in connection with the staff's investigation of Fleming. </FONT></P>

<DL compact>
<DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2><I>Asset impairment and exit costs&#151;</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>As previously discussed, the Company announced a three-year restructuring program
in January&nbsp;2004. During the first nine months and third quarter of 2004, the Company recorded pre-tax asset impairment and exit costs of $482&nbsp;million and $45&nbsp;million,
respectively, relating to the restructuring program and the write-off of intangible assets which were included in operating companies income of the following segments: </FONT></DD></DL>

<UL>
<DL compact>
<DT style='margin-bottom:-11pt;'><FONT SIZE=2>&#149;</FONT></DT><DD><FONT SIZE=2><I>Losses/Gains on Sales of Businesses&#151;</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>During the third quarter of 2004, the Company sold a snack nuts business in
Brazil and recorded a pre-tax loss of $8&nbsp;million. This loss is included in the operating companies income of the Latin America&nbsp;&amp; Asia Pacific segment. During the third quarter of 2003,
the Company sold a European rice business and recorded a pre-tax gain of $23&nbsp;million. This gain is included in the operating companies income of the Europe, Middle East&nbsp;&amp; Africa segment. </FONT></DD></DL>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>As
discussed in Note 8. </FONT><FONT SIZE=2><I>Segment Reporting</I></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>, management uses operating companies income, which is defined as operating income before general corporate
expenses and amortization of intangibles, to evaluate segment performance and allocate resources. Management believes it is appropriate to disclose this measure to help investors analyze the business
performance and trends of the various business segments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Consolidated Results of Operations for the Nine Months Ended September&nbsp;30, 2004  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
following discussion compares consolidated operating results for the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2004 with the nine months ended September&nbsp;30, 2003. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Volume
increased 2.4%, due primarily to acquisitions and increased shipments in the U.S. Cheese, Canada&nbsp;&amp; North America Foodservice segment, partially offset by the impact of divested
businesses. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $1,049&nbsp;million (4.6%), due primarily to favorable currency ($628&nbsp;million), higher volume/mix ($306&nbsp;million), higher net pricing ($110&nbsp;million,
reflecting commodity-driven pricing, partially offset by increased promotional spending) and the impact of acquisitions ($106&nbsp;million), partially offset by the impact of divested businesses
($92&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
income decreased $1,042&nbsp;million (23.0%), due primarily to pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($476&nbsp;million), unfavorable costs, net of higher pricing
($409&nbsp;million, due primarily to higher commodity costs and increased promotional spending), higher marketing, administration and research costs ($221&nbsp;million, including higher benefit
costs), higher fixed manufacturing costs ($41&nbsp;million, including higher benefit costs), the unfavorable net impact related to gains and losses on the sales of businesses ($31&nbsp;million)
and the 2004 implementation costs associated with the restructuring program ($26&nbsp;million), partially offset by higher volume/mix ($103&nbsp;million) and favorable currency
($72&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>32</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<P style='page-break-before:always'></p>
<!-- ZEQ.=3,SEQ=32,EFW="2146084",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=960176,FOLIO='32',FILE='DISK029:[04CHI5.04CHI4315]DU4315A.;7',USER='ABLIJDE',CD=';4-NOV-2004;16:01' -->
<A NAME="page_du4315_1_33"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Currency
movements increased net revenues by $628&nbsp;million and operating income by $72&nbsp;million. These increases were due primarily to the weakness of the U.S. dollar against the euro and
the Canadian dollar. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Interest
and other debt expense, net, decreased $15&nbsp;million, due primarily to lower average debt outstanding. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company's reported effective income tax rate decreased by 3.2 percentage points to 31.9%, resulting from a $76&nbsp;million favorable resolution of an outstanding tax item in the third quarter
of 2004 and the reversal of tax accruals that are no longer required due to tax events that occurred during the first half of 2004. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
earnings of $2,037&nbsp;million decreased $570&nbsp;million (21.9%), due primarily to lower operating income, partially offset by a lower effective income tax rate. Diluted and basic EPS,
which were both $1.19, decreased by 21.2%. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><I>Consolidated Results of Operations for the Three Months Ended September&nbsp;30, 2004  </I></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
following discussion compares consolidated operating results for the three months ended September&nbsp;30, 2004 with the three months ended September&nbsp;30, 2003. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Volume
increased 3.0%, due primarily to acquisitions and increased shipments in the U.S. Cheese, Canada&nbsp;&amp; North America Foodservice segment and U.S. Snacks segment, partially offset by the
impact of divested businesses. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $351&nbsp;million (4.7%), due primarily to higher volume/mix ($202&nbsp;million), favorable currency ($85&nbsp;million), higher net pricing ($62 million, reflecting
commodity-driven price increases, partially offset by higher promotional spending) and the impact of acquisitions ($37&nbsp;million), partially offset by the impact of divested businesses
($26&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
income decreased $157&nbsp;million (11.1%), due primarily to unfavorable costs, net of higher pricing ($106&nbsp;million, reflecting higher commodity costs and increased promotional
spending), higher marketing, administration and research costs ($49&nbsp;million, including higher benefit costs), pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($39&nbsp;million), the
unfavorable net impact related to gains and losses on the sales of businesses ($31&nbsp;million), the 2004 implementation costs associated with the restructuring program ($16&nbsp;million) and
higher fixed manufacturing costs, partially offset by higher volume/mix ($86&nbsp;million) and favorable currency ($10&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>Currency
movements increased net revenues by $85&nbsp;million and operating income by $10&nbsp;million. These increases were due primarily to the weakness of the U.S. dollar against the euro and
the Canadian dollar. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
Company's reported effective income tax rate decreased by 6.7 percentage points to 28.4%, resulting from a $76&nbsp;million favorable resolution of an outstanding tax item. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
earnings of $779&nbsp;million decreased $31&nbsp;million (3.8%), due primarily to lower operating income, partially offset by a lower effective income tax rate. Diluted and basic EPS, which
were both $0.46, decreased by 2.1%. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><U>Operating Results by Business Segment</U>  </B></FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Volume
increased 3.5%, due primarily to acquisitions in the U.S. Beverages&nbsp;&amp; Grocery segment and increased shipments in the U.S. Cheese, Canada&nbsp;&amp; North America Foodservice segment. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $605&nbsp;million (3.8%), due primarily to higher volume/mix ($256&nbsp;million), higher net pricing ($148&nbsp;million, reflecting commodity-driven price increases,
partially offset by increased promotional spending), favorable currency ($125&nbsp;million) and the impact of acquisitions ($85&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $754&nbsp;million (20.2%), due primarily to unfavorable costs, net of higher pricing ($345&nbsp;million, including higher commodity costs and increased
promotional spending), the 2004 pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($307&nbsp;million), higher marketing, administration and research costs ($177&nbsp;million, including higher
benefit costs), the 2004 implementation costs associated with the restructuring program ($22&nbsp;million) and higher fixed manufacturing costs ($19&nbsp;million, including higher benefit costs),
partially offset by higher volume/mix ($98&nbsp;million) and favorable currency ($21&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
following discusses operating results within each of Kraft North America Commercial's reportable segments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>U.S. Beverages&nbsp;&amp; Grocery.</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume increased 5.8%, due primarily to the 2004 acquisition of a beverage business and gains in
enhancers, coffee and desserts, partially offset by a decline in cereals. Beverages volume increased, due primarily to the 2004 acquisition of a beverage business and new product introductions. Volume
also increased in enhancers, primarily mayonnaise and salad dressings, and in coffee, due to product quality improvements and the impact of an expanded distribution arrangement. In desserts, volume
increased, due primarily to higher shipments of refrigerated, ready-to-eat desserts and frozen toppings. In cereals, volume declined driven by health and wellness concerns, which impacted the
category, and increased competitive activities. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $41&nbsp;million (0.9%), due primarily to the impact of acquisitions ($70&nbsp;million) and higher volume/mix ($11&nbsp;million), partially offset by increased promotional
spending, net of higher pricing ($40&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>34</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<P style='page-break-before:always'></p>
<!-- ZEQ.=5,SEQ=34,EFW="2146084",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=546174,FOLIO='34',FILE='DISK029:[04CHI5.04CHI4315]DU4315A.;7',USER='ABLIJDE',CD=';4-NOV-2004;16:01' -->
<A NAME="page_du4315_1_35"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $158&nbsp;million (10.9%), due primarily to unfavorable costs and higher promotional spending ($96&nbsp;million, including higher commodity costs), higher
marketing, administration and research costs ($68&nbsp;million), the 2004 pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($19&nbsp;million) and higher benefit costs, partially offset by lower
fixed manufacturing costs ($16&nbsp;million), higher volume/mix ($7&nbsp;million) and the impact of acquisitions. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>U.S. Snacks.</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume increased 1.1%, as higher salted snacks volume was partially offset by lower biscuits and confectionery volume. Salted
snacks volume increased due to consumer nutrition trends and marketing programs in nuts. In biscuits, volume declined, as consumer health and wellness concerns continued to affect consumption.
Confectionery volume also declined due to category softness and increased competitive activity. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues decreased $27&nbsp;million (0.8%), due primarily to unfavorable volume/mix ($25&nbsp;million) and the 2004 implementation costs associated with the restructuring program
($9&nbsp;million), partially offset by higher pricing ($7&nbsp;million, including the absence of high product returns associated with new products incurred in the prior year, partially offset by
increased promotional spending). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $311&nbsp;million (44.6%), due primarily to the 2004 pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($190&nbsp;million), higher marketing, administration
and research costs ($61&nbsp;million), unfavorable costs, net of higher pricing ($33&nbsp;million, driven by higher commodity costs and increased promotional spending), unfavorable volume/mix
($22&nbsp;million), the 2004 implementation costs associated with the restructuring program ($20&nbsp;million) and higher benefit costs, partially offset by lower fixed manufacturing costs
($17&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>U.S. Cheese, Canada&nbsp;&amp; North America Foodservice.</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume increased 3.5%, due primarily to the impact of acquisitions and higher
volume in foodservice and cheese. Volume in the foodservice business increased, due primarily to an acquisition of a beverage business in 2004 and higher shipments to national accounts. In cheese,
volume also increased, benefiting from increased promotional spending. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $495&nbsp;million (10.1%), due primarily to higher volume/mix ($212&nbsp;million), higher pricing, net of higher promotional reinvestment spending in cheese
($146&nbsp;million, reflecting commodity-driven pricing in cheese and foodservice), favorable currency ($125&nbsp;million) and the impact of acquisitions. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $232&nbsp;million (24.6%), due primarily to unfavorable costs, net of higher pricing ($190&nbsp;million, including higher commodity costs and increased
promotional spending), the 2004 pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($90&nbsp;million), higher fixed manufacturing costs ($46&nbsp;million, including higher benefit costs) and
higher marketing, administration and research costs ($18&nbsp;million), partially offset by higher volume/mix ($92&nbsp;million) and favorable currency ($21&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>U.S. Convenient Meals.</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume increased 0.6%, due primarily to gains in meats, partially offset by lower shipments in meals. Meats volume
increased driven by higher consumption of cold cuts, supported by higher investment spending. In meals, volume declined due to the discontinuation of certain product lines in the second half of 2003. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $96&nbsp;million (3.1%), due primarily to higher volume/mix ($58&nbsp;million), higher pricing, net of increased promotional spending ($35&nbsp;million, reflecting
commodity-driven pricing in meats and pizza), and the impact of acquisitions. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $53&nbsp;million (8.2%), due primarily to higher marketing, administration and research costs ($30&nbsp;million), unfavorable costs, net of higher pricing
($26&nbsp;million, including higher commodity costs and increased promotional spending), the 2004 pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($8&nbsp;million) and higher fixed
manufacturing costs ($6&nbsp;million, including higher benefit costs), partially offset by higher volume/mix ($21 million). </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>35</FONT></P>

<TD WIDTH="2%"><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;</FONT></TD>
<TD COLSPAN=2 ALIGN="RIGHT"><HR NOSHADE SIZE=4></TD>
</TR>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Volume
decreased 0.5%, due primarily to the impact of the divestiture of a rice business and a branded fresh cheese business in Europe in 2003, as well as price competition and trade inventory
reductions in several markets, partially offset by the impact of acquisitions. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $444&nbsp;million (6.6%), due primarily to favorable currency ($503&nbsp;million), favorable volume/mix ($50&nbsp;million) and the impact of acquisitions
($21&nbsp;million), partially offset by the impact of divestitures ($92&nbsp;million) and increased promotional spending, net of higher pricing ($38&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $292&nbsp;million (31.2%), due primarily to the pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($169&nbsp;million), unfavorable costs and
increased promotional spending ($86&nbsp;million), higher marketing, administration and research costs ($44&nbsp;million, including higher benefit costs and infrastructure investment in developing
markets), the unfavorable net impact related to gains and losses on the sales of businesses ($31&nbsp;million) and the impact of divestitures ($16&nbsp;million), partially offset by favorable
currency ($51&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
following discusses operating results within each of Kraft International Commercial's reportable segments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>Europe, Middle East&nbsp;&amp; Africa.</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume decreased 0.4%, due primarily to the divestiture of a rice business and a branded fresh cheese
business in Europe in 2003, price competition, trade inventory reductions in Russia, and lower shipments in France. These declines were partially offset by the impact of acquisitions and volume growth
in Germany, Italy and several Eastern European markets. Beverages volume declined, driven by price competition and trade inventory reductions on coffee in France and lower shipments of refreshment
beverages in the Middle East. Cheese volume also declined, impacted by the divestiture of a branded fresh cheese business in Europe in 2003, partially offset by increased shipments in Germany, Italy
and the United Kingdom. Convenient meals volume declined, impacted by the divestiture of a rice business in Europe in 2003. In grocery, volume increased, due primarily to an acquisition in Egypt.
Snacks volume also increased, due to gains in biscuits, benefiting from acquisitions, new confectionery product introductions across the segment and </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>36</FONT></P>

<P style='page-break-before:always'></p>
<!-- ZEQ.=1,SEQ=36,EFW="2146084",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=1019520,FOLIO='36',FILE='DISK029:[04CHI5.04CHI4315]DW4315A.;5',USER='ABLIJDE',CD=';4-NOV-2004;16:01' -->
<A NAME="page_dw4315_1_37"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>cooler
weather across Europe as compared to the prior year heat wave, partially offset by price competition and trade inventory reductions in some markets. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $403&nbsp;million (8.3%), due primarily to favorable currency ($469&nbsp;million), favorable volume/mix ($67&nbsp;million) and the impact of acquisitions
($21&nbsp;million), partially offset by the impact of divestitures ($91&nbsp;million) and lower pricing and increased promotional spending ($63&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $195&nbsp;million (29.3%), due primarily to the pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($143&nbsp;million), lower pricing and
increased promotional spending ($63&nbsp;million), higher marketing, administration and research costs ($31&nbsp;million, including higher benefit costs as well as infrastructure investment in
developing markets), the 2003 pre-tax gain on the sale of a rice business in Europe ($23&nbsp;million) and the impact of divestitures ($15&nbsp;million), partially offset by favorable
currency ($57&nbsp;million) and favorable volume/mix ($25&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>Latin America&nbsp;&amp; Asia Pacific.</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume decreased 0.7%, due primarily to declines in Mexico, Peru, Venezuela and Southeast Asia,
partially offset by gains in Argentina, Brazil and China. Snacks volume declined, due primarily to lower biscuit shipments in Southeast Asia and biscuit trade inventory reductions in Peru and
Venezuela, partially offset by gains in confectionery in Argentina and Brazil. In grocery, volume also declined, due primarily to the lower results in Asia Pacific. Beverages volume declined, impacted
by price competition in Mexico and lower shipments in Venezuela, partially offset by gains in Brazil and China. Cheese volume increased, due primarily to gains across several markets, including the
Philippines, Mexico and Australia. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $41&nbsp;million (2.2%), due primarily to favorable currency ($34&nbsp;million) and higher pricing ($25&nbsp;million, reflecting devaluation-driven cost increases,
partially offset by increased promotional spending), partially offset by lower volume/mix ($17&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $97&nbsp;million (36.1%), due primarily to the 2004 pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($26&nbsp;million), unfavorable costs, net
of higher pricing ($23&nbsp;million, including increased promotional spending), lower volume/mix ($20&nbsp;million), higher marketing, administration and research costs ($13&nbsp;million), the
2004 pre-tax loss on the sale of a snack nuts business in Brazil and unfavorable currency. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Volume
increased 4.5%, due primarily to acquisitions in the U.S. Beverages&nbsp;&amp; Grocery segment and increased shipments in the U.S Snacks segment, the U.S. Cheese, Canada&nbsp;&amp; North America
Foodservice segment and the U.S. Convenient Meals segment. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $268&nbsp;million (5.2%), due primarily to higher volume/mix ($150&nbsp;million), higher net pricing ($77&nbsp;million, reflecting commodity-driven pricing on cheese,
meats, pizza, cereal and foodservice, partially offset by increased promotional spending), the impact of acquisitions ($37&nbsp;million) and favorable currency ($13&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $50&nbsp;million (4.4%), due primarily to unfavorable costs, net of higher pricing ($76&nbsp;million, including higher commodity costs and increased
promotional spending), higher marketing, administration and research costs ($32&nbsp;million, including higher benefit costs), the 2004 implementation costs associated with the restructuring program
($13&nbsp;million) and the 2004 pre-tax charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($6&nbsp;million), partially offset by higher volume/mix ($72&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
following discusses operating results within each of Kraft North America Commercial's reportable segments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>U.S. Beverages&nbsp;&amp; Grocery.</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume increased 6.9%, due primarily to the 2004 acquisition of a beverage business, partially offset by a
decline in desserts. Beverages volume increased, due primarily to a 2004 acquisition of a beverage business and new product introductions, partially offset by trade inventory reductions and category
softness in ready-to-drink beverages. In coffee, volume increased, benefiting from the impact of </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>38</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<P style='page-break-before:always'></p>
<!-- ZEQ.=1,SEQ=38,EFW="2146084",CP="KRAFT FOODS INC",DN="1",CHK=109077,FOLIO='38',FILE='DISK029:[04CHI5.04CHI4315]DY4315A.;7',USER='ABLIJDE',CD=';4-NOV-2004;16:01' -->
<A NAME="page_dy4315_1_39"> </A>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>an
expanded distribution arrangement. Desserts volume decreased, driven by consumption declines of sugar-based varieties, partially offset by higher shipments of sugar-free products. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $39&nbsp;million (3.0%), due primarily to the impact of acquisitions ($31&nbsp;million) and higher volume/mix ($24&nbsp;million), partially offset by increased promotional
spending, net of higher pricing ($16&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $22&nbsp;million (5.7%), due primarily to unfavorable costs, net of higher pricing ($33&nbsp;million, including higher commodity costs and increased
promotional spending) and higher marketing, administration and research costs ($12&nbsp;million, including higher benefit costs), partially offset by higher volume/mix ($15&nbsp;million) and lower
fixed manufacturing costs. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>U.S. Snacks.</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume increased 3.5%, due primarily to higher biscuits and salted snacks volume, partially offset by lower confectionery
volume. Biscuits volume increased, aided by new product introductions. In salted snacks, volume also increased, benefiting from continued consumer nutrition trends. Confectionery volume declined, due
primarily to category softness and increased competitive activity. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $11&nbsp;million (0.9%), due primarily to higher volume/mix ($27&nbsp;million), partially offset by the 2004 implementation costs associated with the restructuring program
($9&nbsp;million) and lower net pricing ($7&nbsp;million, including increased promotional spending, partially offset by the absence of high product returns associated with new products incurred in
the prior year). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $12&nbsp;million (5.2%), due primarily to the 2004 implementation costs associated with the restructuring program ($12&nbsp;million), unfavorable costs
($11&nbsp;million, including higher commodity costs and increased promotional spending), higher marketing, administration and research costs ($9&nbsp;million) and the 2004 pre-tax
charges for asset impairment and exit costs ($5&nbsp;million), partially offset by lower fixed manufacturing costs ($14&nbsp;million) and higher volume/mix ($12&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>U.S. Cheese, Canada&nbsp;&amp; North America Foodservice.</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume increased 3.3%, due primarily to higher volume in cheese and foodservice. In
cheese, volume increased due primarily to share gains resulting from increased promotional
spending. Volume in the foodservice business also increased, driven by higher shipments to national accounts and the 2004 acquisition of a beverage business. </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $168&nbsp;million (10.2%), due primarily to higher foodservice and cheese pricing, net of higher promotional reinvestment spending in cheese ($85&nbsp;million), higher
volume/mix ($65&nbsp;million), favorable currency ($13&nbsp;million) and the impact of acquisitions. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $3&nbsp;million (1.0%), due primarily to unfavorable costs, net of higher pricing ($26&nbsp;million, including higher commodity costs and increased promotional
spending) and higher fixed manufacturing costs ($19&nbsp;million, including higher benefit costs), partially offset by higher volume/mix ($35&nbsp;million), lower marketing, administration and
research costs and favorable currency ($3&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>U.S. Convenient Meals.</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume increased 2.6%, due primarily to higher shipments in meats and pizza. Meats volume increased driven by gains
in cold cuts and hot dogs. In pizza, volume also increased, aided by new product introductions. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $50&nbsp;million (4.8%), due primarily to higher volume/mix ($34&nbsp;million) and higher pricing, net of increased promotional spending ($15&nbsp;million, reflecting
commodity-driven pricing in meats and pizza). </FONT></P>


<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $13&nbsp;million (5.9%), due primarily to higher marketing, administration and research costs ($16&nbsp;million), unfavorable costs, net of higher pricing
($6&nbsp;million, including higher </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Volume
decreased 0.6%, due primarily to the impact of divestitures and price competition and trade inventory reductions in Latin America, partially offset by growth in the Europe, Middle East&nbsp;&amp;
Africa segment. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Net
revenues increased $83&nbsp;million (3.6%), due primarily to favorable currency ($72&nbsp;million) and favorable volume/mix ($52&nbsp;million), partially offset by the impact of divestitures
($26&nbsp;million) and lower pricing and increased promotional spending ($15&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>Operating
companies income decreased $108&nbsp;million (32.2%), due primarily to unfavorable costs ($42&nbsp;million, including increased promotional spending), the pre-tax charges for
asset impairment and exit costs ($33&nbsp;million), the unfavorable net impact related to gains and losses on the sales of businesses ($31&nbsp;million), higher marketing, administration and
research costs ($17&nbsp;million), the impact of divestitures and the 2004 implementation costs associated with the restructuring program ($3&nbsp;million), partially offset by favorable
volume/mix ($14&nbsp;million) and favorable currency ($7&nbsp;million). </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2>The
following discusses operating results within each of Kraft International Commercial's reportable segments. </FONT></P>

<P><FONT SIZE=2><B><I>Europe, Middle East&nbsp;&amp; Africa.</I></B></FONT><FONT SIZE=2>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Volume increased 1.5%, due primarily to growth in Germany and Russia, partially offset by trade
inventory reductions and price competition in France and the divestiture of a rice business and a branded fresh cheese business in Europe in 2003. Beverages volume increased, as coffee volume
benefited from increased promotional investments in Germany and cooler summer weather across Europe as compared to the prior year heat wave, partially offset by price competition and trade inventory
reductions in France. Snacks volume increased, due primarily to confectionery gains across several markets, benefiting from cooler summer weather across Europe as compared to the prior year heat wave,
increased trade purchases following the second quarter 2004 national transportation strike in Norway and new product introductions. Cheese volume declined, impacted by the divestiture of a branded
fresh cheese business in </FONT></P>

<P ALIGN="CENTER"><FONT SIZE=2>40</FONT></P>

<HR NOSHADE>
<P style='page-break-before:always'></p>
